<p><b>FC Dinamo Tbilisi</b> (<a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a>: <span lang="ka" xml:lang="ka">დინამო თბილისი</span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgian</a> professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team, based in the capital <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a>.</p>
<p>Dinamo Tbilisi was one of the most prominent clubs in Soviet football and a major contender in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">Soviet Top League</a> almost immediately after it was established in <a href="/wiki/1936_Soviet_Top_League" title="1936 Soviet Top League">1936</a>. The club was then part of one of the leading sport societies in <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dynamo_Sports_Club" title="Dynamo Sports Club">All-Union Dynamo sports society</a> which had several other divisions beside football and was sponsored by the Soviet Ministry of Internal Affairs. Its main claim to European fame was winning the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">Cup Winners' Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1981_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup_Final" title="1981 European Cup Winners' Cup Final">1981</a>, beating <a href="/wiki/FC_Carl_Zeiss_Jena" title="FC Carl Zeiss Jena">FC Carl Zeiss Jena</a> of <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> 2–1 in the final in Düsseldorf. Throughout its history, FC Dinamo Tbilisi produced many famous Soviet players: <a href="/wiki/Boris_Paichadze" title="Boris Paichadze">Boris Paichadze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avtandil_Gogoberidze" title="Avtandil Gogoberidze">Avtandil Gogoberidze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shota_Iamanidze" title="Shota Iamanidze">Shota Iamanidze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Meskhi" title="Mikheil Meskhi">Mikheil Meskhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slava_Metreveli" title="Slava Metreveli">Slava Metreveli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murtaz_Khurtsilava" title="Murtaz Khurtsilava">Murtaz Khurtsilava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manuchar_Machaidze" title="Manuchar Machaidze">Manuchar Machaidze</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Kipiani" title="David Kipiani">David Kipiani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Gutsaev" title="Vladimir Gutsaev">Vladimir Gutsaev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandre_Chivadze" title="Aleksandre Chivadze">Aleksandre Chivadze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitaly_Daraselia" title="Vitaly Daraselia">Vitaly Daraselia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ramaz_Shengelia" title="Ramaz Shengelia">Ramaz Shengelia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tengiz_Sulakvelidze" title="Tengiz Sulakvelidze">Tengiz Sulakvelidze</a>. After the break-up of the Soviet Union, it would later produce some of the finest Georgian players such as <a href="/wiki/Temur_Ketsbaia" title="Temur Ketsbaia">Temur Ketsbaia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shota_Arveladze" title="Shota Arveladze">Shota Arveladze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Kinkladze" title="Georgi Kinkladze">Giorgi Kinkladze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kakha_Kaladze" title="Kakha Kaladze">Kakha Kaladze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Levan_Kobiashvili" title="Levan Kobiashvili">Levan Kobiashvili</a>.</p>
<p>Dinamo Tbilisi was one of a handful of teams in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">Soviet Top League</a> (along with <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Moscow" title="FC Dynamo Moscow">Dynamo Moscow</a>) that were never relegated. Their most famous coach was <a href="/wiki/Nodar_Akhalkatsi" title="Nodar Akhalkatsi">Nodar Akhalkatsi</a>, who led the team to the Soviet title in <a href="/wiki/1978_Soviet_Top_League" title="1978 Soviet Top League">1978</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Cup" title="Soviet Cup">Soviet cups</a> (<a href="/wiki/1976_Soviet_Cup_Final" title="1976 Soviet Cup Final">1976</a> and <a href="/wiki/1979_Soviet_Cup_Final" title="1979 Soviet Cup Final">1979</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">UEFA Cup Winners' Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1981_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup_Final" title="1981 European Cup Winners' Cup Final">1981</a>. He was also one of three co-coaches of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_national_football_team" title="Soviet Union national football team">Soviet Union national football team</a> during the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982</a>. FC Dinamo Tbilisi are also 16–time <a href="/wiki/Umaglesi_Liga" title="Umaglesi Liga">Georgian league</a> champions and 13–time <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Cup" title="Georgian Cup">Georgian Cup</a> holders (the current records).</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Beginning:_1920s">The Beginning: 1920s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The Beginning: 1920s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The history of FC Dinamo Tbilisi began in autumn 1925 when the <a href="/wiki/Dynamo_Sports_Club" title="Dynamo Sports Club">Dinamo sports society</a> set out to form a football club, at a time when football was gradually becoming one of the most popular sports in the world.</p>
<p>In 1927, FC Dinamo Tbilisi established a Junior club, "<a href="/wiki/FC_Norchi_Dinamo_Tbilisi" title="FC Norchi Dinamo Tbilisi">Norchi Dinamoeli</a>" (young Dinamo). The Juniors club provided senior with many young skillful players, including the first goalkeeper who played for Dinamo in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">USSR championship</a>, the first captain Shota Savgulidze, defender Mikhail Minaev, forward Vladimer Berdzenishvili and other famous players.</p>
<p>In the early years in Georgia no official championship existed, so the teams played friendly games against each other. The first match was played with <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> team Dinamo Baku on 26 January 1926, with the more experienced Azerbaijan squad winning 1–0. The Dinamo team starred: D.Tsomaia, A.Pochkhua, M.Blackman, I.Foidorov, N.Anakin, A.Gonel, A.Pivovarov, O.Goldobin, A.Galperin, S.Maslenikov, V.Tsomaia.</p>
<p>Three days later, Dinamo played another Azerbaijan team, "Progress" and easily beat them 3–0.</p>
<p>Despite their success in the middle years of the 1930s, the <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Football Federation of the Soviet Union">football federation of the Soviet Union</a> placed FC Dinamo Tbilisi in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_First_League" title="Soviet First League">first league</a> instead of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">Top League</a>. Dinamo continued to show good form against the top teams, winning 9–5 in Tbilisi against probably the best team in the USSR championship, <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Moscow" title="FC Dynamo Moscow">Dynamo Moscow</a>. They later beat <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Saint_Petersburg" title="FC Dynamo Saint Petersburg">Dinamo Leningrad</a> 3–2, winning 5 matches out of 6 plus a draw against Stalinec Moscow. This was enough for Dinamo to qualify for the top League.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II:_1930s_and_1940s">World War II: 1930s and 1940s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: World War II: 1930s and 1940s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The second championship started in autumn <a href="/wiki/1936_Soviet_Top_League" title="1936 Soviet Top League">1936</a>. Altogether Dinamo played 1424 matches in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">Soviet Union Championship</a>. The first match was against <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a>, finishing 2–2, with goals by Nikolas Somov and <a href="/wiki/Boris_Paichadze" title="Boris Paichadze">Boris Paichadze</a>. The team sheet was: A.Dorokhov, S.Shavgulidze (E.Nikolaishvili), B.Berdzenishvili, N.Anakin, V.Jorbenadze, G.Gagua, I.Panin, M.Berdzenishvili, B.Paichadze, M.Aslamazov and N.Somov.</p>
<p>The first victory in the USSR championship was in the match against <a href="/wiki/FC_Spartak_Moscow" title="FC Spartak Moscow">Spartak Moscow</a> on 25 September with Mikheil Berdzenishvili scoring the winning goal. Dinamo finished the season in 3rd place. They challenged for the title, but this faded after the 2–3 loss against <a href="/wiki/FC_Elektrosila_Leningrad" title="FC Elektrosila Leningrad">Krasnaia Zaria Leningrad</a>. Dinamo also played an unforgettable match in Moscow against <a href="/wiki/FC_Spartak_Moscow" title="FC Spartak Moscow">Spartak Moscow</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Cup" title="Soviet Cup">Soviet Cup</a> quarter-final, when Dinamo beat them 6–3. They reached the first edition of Soviet Cup <a href="/wiki/1936_Soviet_Cup_Final" title="1936 Soviet Cup Final">final</a>, but lost 0–2 to <a href="/wiki/FC_Lokomotiv_Moscow" title="FC Lokomotiv Moscow">Lokomotiv Moscow</a>. Their first international match was against the Spanish team <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_national_football_team" title="Basque Country national football team">Baskonia</a> in 1937, which Dinamo lost 0–2.</p>
<p>In the 1930s and 1940s, Dinamo was one of the top Soviet football teams, even though they did not win a title. They were often referred to as the "crownless champions" with the team including: S.Shavgulidze, A.Dorokhov, S.Shudra, B.Frolov, M.Berdzenishvili, A.Kiknadze, V.Panjukov, V.Berezhnoi, G.Gagua, V.Jorbenadze, G.Jejelava.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1950s">1950s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1950s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1950s, the team was led by <a href="/wiki/Avtandil_Gogoberidze" title="Avtandil Gogoberidze">Avtandil Gogoberidze</a> who spent 14 years with Dinamo. He still holds the record for games played and goals scored for Dinamo, with 341 matches and 127 goals. In the same period, the following players starred for Dinamo: G.Antadze, Vladimer Marghania, N.Dziapshipa, M.Minaev, A.Zazroev, V.Eloshvili, <a href="/wiki/Avtandil_Chkuaseli" title="Avtandil Chkuaseli">Avtandil Chkuaseli</a>.</p>
<p>A prominent place in Dinamo history belongs to Andro Jordania, a coach who is considered as one most important figures in the club's history. His period in charge was seen as "the Renaissance" of Dinamo's traditions, which laid the ground for the major successes connected with his name. The club's Digomi practice ground is named after his name.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Soviet_successes:_1960s">First Soviet successes: 1960s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: First Soviet successes: 1960s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first major success came in <a href="/wiki/1964_Soviet_Top_League" title="1964 Soviet Top League">1964 Soviet Top League</a> when Dinamo won the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">Soviet Top League</a>, with the team unbeaten in the last 15 matches. At the end, Dinamo was tied with <a href="/wiki/FC_Torpedo_Moscow" title="FC Torpedo Moscow">Torpedo Moscow</a> so the teams played an additional match in <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>, which Dinamo won 4–1. Georgian supporters celebrated the victory by naming their team <i>"Golden Guys"</i>.</p>
<p>A popular <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> magazine <a href="/wiki/France_Football" title="France Football">France Football</a> wrote: " Dinamo has great players. Their technique, skills and playing intellect enables us to name them the best Eastern representatives of 'South American Football Traditions', if Dinamo were able to participate in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA European Cup</a>, we are certain, they would bring the hegemony of Spanish-Italian teams to an end." However, no Soviet team appeared in the European Cup at that time.</p>
<p>The line-up of winning team in 1964 was: <a href="/wiki/Sergo_Kotrikadze" title="Sergo Kotrikadze">Sergo Kotrikadze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giorgi_Sichinava" title="Giorgi Sichinava">Giorgi Sichinava</a>, Guram Petriashvili, Jemal Zeinklishvili, <a href="/wiki/Guram_Tskhovrebov" title="Guram Tskhovrebov">Guram Tskhovrebov</a>, Vladimer Rekhviashvili, <a href="/wiki/Shota_Iamanidze" title="Shota Iamanidze">Shota Iamanidze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slava_Metreveli" title="Slava Metreveli">Slava Metreveli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimer_Barkaia" title="Vladimer Barkaia">Vladimer Barkaia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Meskhi" title="Mikheil Meskhi">Mikheil Meskhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilia_Datunashvili" title="Ilia Datunashvili">Ilia Datunashvili</a>, Alexander Apshiev. Coach: <a href="/wiki/Gavriil_Kachalin" title="Gavriil Kachalin">Gavriil Kachalin</a>.</p>
<p>In the late 1960s and early 1970s, the quality of the Dinamo team was further enhanced by several skillful players: <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Meskhi" title="Mikheil Meskhi">Mikheil Meskhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slava_Metreveli" title="Slava Metreveli">Slava Metreveli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murtaz_Khurtsilava" title="Murtaz Khurtsilava">Murtaz Khurtsilava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Revaz_Dzodzuashvili" title="Revaz Dzodzuashvili">Revaz Dzodzuashvili</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kakhi_Asatiani" title="Kakhi Asatiani">Kakhi Asatiani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gocha_Gavasheli" title="Gocha Gavasheli">Gocha Gavasheli</a>, Guram Petriashvili, Piruz Kanteladze and the brothers Nodia.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_years:_1970s">European years: 1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: European years: 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dinamo's first appearance in Europe was in <a href="/wiki/1972%E2%80%9373_UEFA_Cup" title="1972–73 UEFA Cup">1972</a> against Dutch team <a href="/wiki/FC_Twente" title="FC Twente">Twente</a> in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a>. Dinamo won the game 3–2,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> with two goals scored by <a href="/wiki/Givi_Nodia" title="Givi Nodia">Givi Nodia</a> and one by <a href="/wiki/David_Kipiani" title="David Kipiani">David Kipiani</a>. The following players appeared on the field in this historic match: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=David_Gogia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="David Gogia (page does not exist)">David Gogia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Revaz_Dzodzuashvili" title="Revaz Dzodzuashvili">Revaz Dzodzuashvili</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vakhtang_Chelidze&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vakhtang Chelidze (page does not exist)">Vakhtang Chelidze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murtaz_Khurtsilava" title="Murtaz Khurtsilava">Murtaz Khurtsilava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shota_Khinchagashvili" title="Shota Khinchagashvili">Shota Khinchagashvili</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Guram_Petriashvili&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Guram Petriashvili (page does not exist)">Guram Petriashvili</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manuchar_Machaidze" title="Manuchar Machaidze">Manuchar Machaidze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kakhi_Asatiani" title="Kakhi Asatiani">Kakhi Asatiani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Gutsaev" title="Vladimir Gutsaev">Vladimir Gutsaev</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Levan_Nodia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Levan Nodia (page does not exist)">Levan Nodia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Givi_Nodia" title="Givi Nodia">Givi Nodia</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Kipiani" title="David Kipiani">David Kipiani</a>. In the second match Twente won the game 2–0 and progressed to the next round.</p>
<p>In 1973 Dinamo won their first International tournament. After beating <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">Benfica</a>, the club won the Columbus's Caravela Trophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1976 <a href="/wiki/Nodar_Akhalkatsi" title="Nodar Akhalkatsi">Nodar Akhalkatsi</a> was appointed as Dinamo's head coach. It was under his leadership that Dinamo achieved greatest success. The club was referred as the "Great Team" between 1976–82, characterised by a mobile, fast and technical style of play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In this period Dinamo won the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Cup" title="Soviet Cup">Soviet Cup</a> for the first time in their history, convincingly defeating Armenian side <a href="/wiki/FC_Ararat_Yerevan" title="FC Ararat Yerevan">Ararat Yerevan</a> 3–0 in the <a href="/wiki/1976_Soviet_Cup_Final" title="1976 Soviet Cup Final">final</a>, with goals scored by <a href="/wiki/David_Kipiani" title="David Kipiani">David Kipiani</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Piruz_Kanteladze&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Piruz Kanteladze (page does not exist)">Piruz Kanteladze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Revaz_Chelebadze" title="Revaz Chelebadze">Revaz Chelebadze</a>. In <a href="/wiki/1978_Soviet_Top_League" title="1978 Soviet Top League">1978</a> the club won the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">Soviet Top League</a> for a second time. Next year Dinamo won Soviet Cup again by defeating Russian side <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Moscow" title="FC Dynamo Moscow">Dynamo Moscow</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1979_Soviet_Cup_Final" title="1979 Soviet Cup Final">final</a>. In <a href="/wiki/1979%E2%80%9380_European_Cup" title="1979–80 European Cup">1979</a> the club played its first match in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA European Cup</a> tournament. In the first round Dinamo knocked out English side <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, at the time one of the strongest teams in European football. After losing the first match at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a> 1–2,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Dinamo comfortably beat the opponent 3–0<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> in Tbilisi and advanced to the next round, where they were eliminated by German champions <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburg</a>. In the 70's Dinamo also eliminated famous Italian sides <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> and <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a> in European competitions.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Last_Soviet_Days:_1980s">Last Soviet Days: 1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Last Soviet Days: 1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px">
<div style="position: relative;font-size:80%">
<p><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg"><img alt="Soccer Field Transparant.svg" data-file-height="684" data-file-width="452" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg/200px-Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg/300px-Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg/400px-Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a></p>

<div style="position:absolute; z-index:2; top:18%; left:73%; height: 0; width: 0; margin: 0; padding: 0;">

<div style="position:relative; text-align:center; left: -5em; top:-0.65em; width:10em; line-height:1.4em; white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/David_Kipiani" title="David Kipiani"><b>Kipiani</b></a></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute; z-index:2; top:82%; left:50%; height: 0; width: 0; margin: 0; padding: 0;">
<div style="position:relative; text-align:center; left: -5em; top:-0.65em; width:10em; line-height:1.4em; white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Ramaz_Shengelia" title="Ramaz Shengelia"><b>Shengelia</b></a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align:center; font-size:smaller">Dinamo's famous 1981 title-winning squad.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The highlight of Dinamo's history was winning <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1980–81 European Cup Winners' Cup">1980–81 European Cup Winners' Cup</a>, including knocking out clubs like <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> (4–1,0–1) <a href="/wiki/Feyenoord" title="Feyenoord">Feynoord Rotterdam</a> (3–0,0–2) and beating East German side <a href="/wiki/FC_Carl_Zeiss_Jena" title="FC Carl Zeiss Jena">Carl Zeiss Jena</a> 2–1 in the <a href="/wiki/1981_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup_Final" title="1981 European Cup Winners' Cup Final">final</a> on May 13, 1981. <a href="/wiki/Vitaly_Daraselia" title="Vitaly Daraselia">Vitaly Daraselia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Gutsaev" title="Vladimir Gutsaev">Vladimir Gutsaev</a> scored goals in the final.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stamps_of_Georgia,_2002-17.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="279" data-file-width="359" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Stamps_of_Georgia%2C_2002-17.jpg/200px-Stamps_of_Georgia%2C_2002-17.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Stamps_of_Georgia%2C_2002-17.jpg/300px-Stamps_of_Georgia%2C_2002-17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/33/Stamps_of_Georgia%2C_2002-17.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stamps_of_Georgia,_2002-17.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dinamo Tbilisi, winner of 1981 European Cup Winners' Cup on stamp of Georgia, 2002</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Helmut_Sch%C3%B6n" title="Helmut Schön">Helmut Schön</a>, <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974 FIFA World Cup</a> winning coach said: <i>"It is to be said directly, Dinamo deserved the victory. This team has top quality performers."</i></p>
<p>Next year in <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1981–82 European Cup Winners' Cup">1982</a> as reigning champions Dinamo advanced to the semi-finals in Cup Winners` Cup tournament, where they were eliminated by belgian side <a href="/wiki/Standard_Li%C3%A8ge" title="Standard Liège">Standard Liège</a>. In the 1980s numerous skillful players appeared in the team, but for various reasons they were not able to do their best: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Grigol_Tsaava&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Grigol Tsaava (page does not exist)">Grigol Tsaava</a>, Mikheil Meskhi (Junior), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otar_Korghalidze" title="Otar Korghalidze">Otar Korghalidze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gia_Guruli" title="Gia Guruli">Gia Guruli</a>, Mamuka Pantsulaia, <a href="/wiki/Merab_Jordania" title="Merab Jordania">Merab Jordania</a>, Levan Baratashvili and many other talented players.</p>
<p>From 1983 a crisis began. It was hard for the club to qualify from the first rounds of the Soviet Cup. They also performed poorly in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">championship</a>. From 1983 to 1989 the team appeared only <a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_UEFA_Cup" title="1987–88 UEFA Cup">once</a> in the UEFA tournaments.</p>
<p>Dinamo Tbilisi played its last game in the <a href="/wiki/1989_Soviet_Top_League" title="1989 Soviet Top League">Soviet Top League</a> on 27 October 1989 against Dynamo Kyiv. Dinamo played its first and last official matches in Soviet championship with Dynamo Kyiv, with both matches ending 2–2.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1990 the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Football_Federation" title="Georgian Football Federation">Georgian Football Federation</a> refused to participate in the <a href="/wiki/1990_Soviet_Top_League" title="1990 Soviet Top League">Soviet Union championship</a>. That meant that no Georgian Football Clubs would appear in Soviet tournaments. From that moment the more recent history of FC Dinamo Tbilisi began.</p>
<p>During this time, as a means of distancing from the soviet past, the club was renamed to Iberia Tbilisi. This move was largely opposed by the supporters and by 1992 the club returned to its initial name.</p>
<p>The club played its first match in the <a href="/wiki/1990_Umaglesi_Liga" title="1990 Umaglesi Liga">Georgian National championship</a> against <a href="/wiki/FC_Kolkheti-1913_Poti" title="FC Kolkheti-1913 Poti">Kolkheti Poti</a> on March 30, 1990. Dinamo lost the historic match, 0–1. Ultimately the club recovered from this setback and won the first Georgian National championship. The club also won the next 9 championships.</p>
<p>In 1992 came Dinamo's first double: the team won league and <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Cup" title="Georgian Cup">Georgian Cup</a> beating <a href="/wiki/FC_Tskhumi_Sukhumi" title="FC Tskhumi Sukhumi">Tskhumi Sokhumi</a> in the final. In <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_UEFA_Champions_League" title="1993–94 UEFA Champions League">1993</a> Dinamo played its first international official match representing independent Georgia. Dinamo won the home match against <a href="/wiki/Linfield_F.C." title="Linfield F.C.">Linfield</a> 2–1, with goals from <a href="/wiki/Shota_Arveladze" title="Shota Arveladze">Shota Arveladze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gela_Inalishvili" title="Gela Inalishvili">Gela Inalishvili</a>. The second leg in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> ended 1–1. However the club was disqualified for attempting to bribe the referee in the first leg.</p>
<p>Despite continued success in national cups and championships, the club had no success in European club tournaments.</p>
<p>In 1996 Dinamo passed 3 rounds in the <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_UEFA_Cup" title="1996–97 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a>. They beat <a href="/wiki/CS_Grevenmacher" title="CS Grevenmacher">CS Grevenmacher</a> 4–0, 2–2, <a href="/wiki/Molde_FK" title="Molde FK">Molde FK</a> 2–1, 0–0 and <a href="/wiki/FC_Torpedo_Moscow" title="FC Torpedo Moscow">Torpedo Moscow</a> 1–0, 1–1. In the next round the club was unable to overcome <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> side <a href="/wiki/Boavista_F.C." title="Boavista F.C.">Boavista</a> and left the tournament.</p>
<p>Dinamo came very close to advance in <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_UEFA_Champions_League" title="1998–99 UEFA Champions League">1998–99 UEFA Champions League</a> group stages, but were eliminated by <a href="/wiki/Athletic_Bilbao" title="Athletic Bilbao">Athletic Bilbao</a> on away goals rule 2–1, 0–1. The migration of key players to European clubs caused negative results. It became harder and harder for the club to win the Georgian Championship or Georgian Cup.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the early 2000s, famous Georgian businessman <a href="/wiki/Badri_Patarkatsishvili" title="Badri Patarkatsishvili">Badri Patarkatsishvili</a> purchased FC Dinamo Tbilisi. In 2003 the club won the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Umaglesi_Liga" title="2002–03 Umaglesi Liga">Georgian Championship</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Cup" title="Georgian Cup">Georgian Cup</a>.</p>
<p>In 2004 Dinamo under the leadership of Croatian coach <a href="/wiki/Ivo_%C5%A0u%C5%A1ak" title="Ivo Šušak">Ivo Šušak</a>, won the <a href="/wiki/2004_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States_Cup" title="2004 Commonwealth of Independent States Cup">CIS Cup</a> in Moscow, beating Latvian side <a href="/wiki/Skonto_FC" title="Skonto FC">Skonto</a> 3–1 in the final. Same year, Dinamo successfully made it through the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_UEFA_Cup" title="2004–05 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> qualifying rounds, after defeating <a href="/wiki/FC_BATE_Borisov" title="FC BATE Borisov">BATE Borisov</a> (1–0; 3–2), <a href="/wiki/SK_Slavia_Prague" title="SK Slavia Prague">Slavia Prague</a> (2–0; 1–3) and <a href="/wiki/Wis%C5%82a_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Wisła Kraków">Wisła Kraków</a> (2–1, 3–4) and qualified for the group stage, where their opponents were <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sporting_Clube_de_Portugal" title="Sporting Clube de Portugal">Sporting CP</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Sochaux-Montb%C3%A9liard" title="FC Sochaux-Montbéliard">Sochaux</a> and <a href="/wiki/Panionios_G.S.S." title="Panionios G.S.S.">Panionios</a>. Dinamo lost all four games and finished bottom in the group.</p>
<p>In the following season Dinamo were again <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Umaglesi_Liga" title="2004–05 Umaglesi Liga">Georgian champions</a> and they won the Georgian championship again in <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Umaglesi_Liga" title="2007–08 Umaglesi Liga">2008</a>, when the head coach of Dinamo was Czech <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Uhrin" title="Dušan Uhrin">Dušan Uhrin</a>.</p>
<p>In 2009 the club beat <a href="/wiki/FC_Metalurgi_Rustavi" title="FC Metalurgi Rustavi">Olimpi Rustavi</a> and won the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Georgian_Cup" title="2008–09 Georgian Cup">Georgian Cup</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2011, FC Dinamo Tbilisi was purchased by Georgian businessman <a href="/wiki/Roman_Pipia" title="Roman Pipia">Roman Pipia</a>. That year, the club successfully played in the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2011–12 UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> qualifying rounds, but they were not able to overcome <a href="/wiki/AEK_Athens_F.C." title="AEK Athens F.C.">AEK Athens</a> in the play-off round.</p>
<p>After a bad performance in the Georgian championship of <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Umaglesi_Liga" title="2011–12 Umaglesi Liga">2011–12</a>, Dinamo could not qualify for any UEFA competitions for the first time. The new owner immediately started the modernization of the club<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> starting with the reconstruction of the Digomi training ground. The <a href="/wiki/Boris_Paichadze_Dinamo_Arena" title="Boris Paichadze Dinamo Arena">Boris Paichadze Dinamo Arena</a> was reconstructed as well. The pitch surface was changed with a new specially adapted surface for the local climate. Renovated Youths Football Academy also began its functioning.</p>
<p>The club were beaten 5–0<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a> play-off round in 1st leg and again 3–0<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> the following week at <a href="/wiki/White_Hart_Lane" title="White Hart Lane">White Hart Lane</a>, thus crashing out 8–0 on aggregate.</p>
<p>After that in national competitions Dinamo won the double in 2013, 2014 and 2016 seasons.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dinamo Tbilisi is by far the most successful football club in <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> having won championship 16 and cup 13 times. Dinamo also was one of the major football clubs in Soviet football, that has never been relegated from the top league and alongside Ukrainian <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a> was the only club in Soviet era to win European competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Competitions">European Competitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: European Competitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</ul>

<p><b>European Championship winners</b></p>
<p>Three players have won the <a href="/wiki/1960_European_Nations%27_Cup" title="1960 European Nations' Cup">1960</a> European Championship whilst at Dinamo Tbilisi</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union"><img alt="Soviet Union" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Givi_Chokheli" title="Givi Chokheli">Givi Chokheli</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union"><img alt="Soviet Union" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Zaur_Kaloev" title="Zaur Kaloev">Zaur Kaloev</a></li>

<p><b>Olympic gold medalists</b></p>
<p>One player has won the Seoul <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1988_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1988 Summer Olympics">1988</a> Olympic gold medal whilst in Dinamo Tbilisi</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union"><img alt="Soviet Union" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Gela_Ketashvili" title="Gela Ketashvili">Gela Ketashvili</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Construction of the <a href="/wiki/Boris_Paichadze_Dinamo_Arena" title="Boris Paichadze Dinamo Arena">Dinamo stadium</a> started in autumn 1929 although the project was soon suspended. The construction was renewed in 1933 (chief architect – Archil Kurdiani). Finally it finished on October 12, 1935 and envisaged 23 000 spectators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1960–1962 the stadium was reconstructed and the number of spectators increased to 36 000. After reconstruction the stadium was officially opened on July 27, 1962. Dinamo Tbilisi hosted FC Dynamo Leningrad in Soviet championship and defeated it with minimal score 1–0.</p>
<p>The demand for a new and bigger stadium had increased due to the successful performance of Dinamo Tbilisi. This was the Communist time, when every problem had to be solved by the USSR supreme government body. The leader and the first secretary of Georgian Communist Party <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Shevardnadze" title="Eduard Shevardnadze">Eduard Shevardnadze</a> was able to persuade Official Moscow, that Georgia needed bigger and better stadium for home matches. By the time stadium was built, it took the third place with its capacity in <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. It could fit 78,000 supporters and fulfill every standards and requirements of <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Football Federation of the Soviet Union">Soviet Football Federation</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>.</p>
<p>The first official match played after stadium was built occurred on 29 September 1976. This was UEFA Cup Winners' Cup 1/16 final match between Dinamo Tbilisi and <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a>. Dinamo won the opening game 3–0.</p>
<p>The next reconstruction of the stadium was held in 2006 (architects-Gia Kurdiani and Archil Kurdiani Junior) and number of spectators was changed to 54,549. The stadium was opened with European championship <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008_qualifying_Group_B" title="UEFA Euro 2008 qualifying Group B">qualifying</a> match. On September 6, 2006 Georgian national team hosted French national <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">team</a> and was defeated with the score 3–0. In 2012 the turf of Dinamo Arena was changed. Energy and irrigation systems were also fully rehabilitated. The new lighting was made that satisfied demands of high standards. VIP box has fully changed and fixed according to UEFA standards.</p>
<p>Even though stadium's maximum capacity was 78,000, Georgian football fans can remember matches with more accommodation. For instance, in 1979 Dinamo was hosting one of the best British teams – <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>. The first match was played in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a>, that Liverpool won 2–1. Stadium was attended by 110,000 people and their support played important role in winning. Dinamo beat Liverpool 3–0 and qualified in the next round. In Soviet Union Dinamo stadium is record keeper of the average attendance of 45,000.</p>
<p>The record attendance was repeated in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996_qualifying_Group_7" title="UEFA Euro 1996 qualifying Group 7">1995</a> for <a href="/wiki/Georgia_national_football_team" title="Georgia national football team">Georgia</a> vs <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a>. The football clubs <a href="/wiki/FC_Spartak_Moscow" title="FC Spartak Moscow">Spartak Moscow</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a> often played their autumn international matches on this stadium.</p>
<p>Hundreds of Georgian, European and even South American stars played in Dinamo stadium. In 1985 the stadium hosted the qualifying stage of the <a href="/wiki/1985_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="1985 FIFA World Youth Championship">Juniors World Cup</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cl%C3%A1udio_Taffarel" title="Cláudio Taffarel">Cláudio Taffarel</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCller_(footballer)" title="Müller (footballer)">Muller</a> played for the <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazilian national team</a>.</p>
<p>In 1995 the stadium was renamed Boris Paichadze National Stadium after a major Georgian international <a href="/wiki/Boris_Paichadze" title="Boris Paichadze">footballer</a>. It is home to the <a href="/wiki/Georgia_national_football_team" title="Georgia national football team">Georgia national football team</a>. Holding lit torches, 80,000 fans came in 1981 to congratulate the team on their European Cup Winners Cup triumph.</p>
<p>The stadium hosted <a href="/wiki/2015_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2015 UEFA Super Cup">2015 UEFA Super Cup</a> match between <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla</a>, that Barcelona won 5–4 in extra time.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasons">Seasons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Dinamo_Tbilisi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Seasons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Key</b></p>
<div>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 33.33%;text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
<li>P = Played</li>
<li>W = Games won</li>
<li>D = Games drawn</li>
<li>L = Games lost</li>
<li>F = Goals for</li>
<li>A = Goals against</li>
<li>Pts = Points</li>
<li>Pos = Final position</li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width: 33.33%;text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
<li>UML = <a href="/wiki/Umaglesi_Liga" title="Umaglesi Liga">Umaglesi Liga</a></li>
<li>STL = <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">Soviet Top League</a></li>
<li>SFL = <a href="/wiki/Soviet_First_League" title="Soviet First League">Soviet First League</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width: 33.33%;text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
<li>R1 = First Round</li>
<li>R2 = Second Round</li>
<li>R3 = Third Round</li>
<li>QF = Quarter-finals</li>
<li>SF = Semi-finals</li>
<li>GS = Group Stage</li>
<li>QR1 = First Qualifying Round</li>
<li>QR2 = Second Qualifying Round</li>
<li>QR3 = Third Qualifying Round</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
